If the host is unspecified, the Ingress routes all\n454: \t// traffic based on the specified IngressRuleValue.\n455: \t//\n456: \t// host can be \"precise\" which is a domain name without the terminating dot of\n457: \t// a network host (e.g. \"foo.bar.com\") or \"wildcard\", which is a domain name\n458: \t// prefixed with a single wildcard label (e.g. \"*.foo.com\").\n459: \t// The wildcard character '*' must appear by itself as the first DNS label and\n460: \t// matches only a single label. You cannot have a wildcard label by itself (e.g. Host == \"*\").\n461: \t// Requests will be matched against the host field in the following way:\n462: \t// 1. If host is precise, the request matches this rule if the http host header is equal to Host.\n463: \t// 2. If host is a wildcard, then the request matches this rule if the http host header\n464: \t// is to equal to the suffix (removing the first label) of the wildcard rule.\n465: \t// +optional\n466: \tHost string\n467: \n468: \t// IngressRuleValue represents a rule to route requests for this\n469: \t// IngressRule. If unspecified, the rule defaults to a http catch-all.\n470: \t// Whether that sends just traffic matching the host to the default backend\n471: \t// or all traffic to the default backend, is left to the controller\n472: \t// fulfilling the Ingress. Http is currently the only supported\n473: \t// IngressRuleValue.\n474: \t// +optional\n475: \tIngressRuleValue\n476: }\n477: \n478: // IngressRuleValue represents a rule to apply against incoming requests. If the\n479: // rule is satisfied, the request is routed to the specified backend. Currently\n480: // mixing different types of rules in a single Ingress is disallowed, so exactly\n481: // one of the following must be set.\n482: type IngressRuleValue struct {\n483: \t//TODO:\n484: \t// 1. Consider renaming this resource and the associated rules so they\n485: \t// aren't tied to Ingress. They can be used to route intra-cluster traffic.\n486: \t// 2. Consider adding fields for ingress-type specific global options\n487: \t// usable by a loadbalancer, like http keep-alive.\n488: \n489: \t// +optional\n490: \tHTTP *HTTPIngressRuleValue\n491: }\n492: \n493: // HTTPIngressRuleValue is a list of http selectors pointing to backends.\n494: // In the example: http://<host>/<path>?<searchpart> -> backend where\n495: // where parts of the url correspond to RFC 3986, this resource will be used\n496: // to match against everything after the last '/' and before the first '?'\n497: // or '#'.\n498: type HTTPIngressRuleValue struct {\n499: \t// paths is a collection of paths that map requests to backends.\n500: \t// +listType=atomic\n501: \tPaths []HTTPIngressPath\n502: \t// TODO: Consider adding fields for ingress-type specific global\n503: \t// options usable by a loadbalancer, like http keep-alive.\n504: }\n505: \n506: // PathType represents the type of path referred to by a HTTPIngressPath.\n507: type PathType string\n508: \n509: const (\n510: \t// PathTypeExact matches the URL path exactly and with case sensitivity.\n511: \tPathTypeExact = PathType(\"Exact\")\n512: \n513: \t// PathTypePrefix matches based on a URL path prefix split by '/'. Matching\n514: \t// is case sensitive and done on a path element by element basis. A path\n515: \t// element refers to the list of labels in the path split by the '/'\n516: \t// separator. A request is a match for path p if every p is an element-wise\n517: \t// prefix of p of the request path. Note that if the last element of the\n518: \t// path is a substring of the last element in request path, it is not a\n519: \t// match (e.g. /foo/bar matches /foo/bar/baz, but does not match\n520: \t// /foo/barbaz). If multiple matching paths exist in an Ingress spec, the\n521: \t// longest matching path is given priority.\n522: \t// Examples:\n523: \t// - /foo/bar does not match requests to /foo/barbaz\n524: \t// - /foo/bar matches request to /foo/bar and /foo/bar/baz\n525: \t// - /foo and /foo/ both match requests to /foo and /foo/. If both paths are\n526: \t//   present in an Ingress spec, the longest matching path (/foo/) is given\n527: \t//   priority.\n528: \tPathTypePrefix = PathType(\"Prefix\")\n529: \n530: \t// PathTypeImplementationSpecific matching is up to the IngressClass.\n531: \t// Implementations can treat this as a separate PathType or treat it\n532: \t// identically to Prefix or Exact path types.\n533: \tPathTypeImplementationSpecific = PathType(\"ImplementationSpecific\")\n534: )\n535: \n536: // HTTPIngressPath associates a path with a backend. Incoming urls matching the\n537: // path are forwarded to the backend.\n538: type HTTPIngressPath struct {\n539: \t// path is matched against the path of an incoming request. Currently it can\n540: \t// contain characters disallowed from the conventional \"path\" part of a URL\n541: \t// as defined by RFC 3986.
